  • P2 (Project Control Framework System): The rigid workflow engine that enforces PCF stages. It acts as a constraint on agility. Project Managers spend more time feeding P2 to get 'Green' operational metrics than managing actual site risks. It creates a 'watermelon' status reporting culture (green on the outside, red on the inside).
  • dIMS (Digital Integrated Management System): The central repository for asset inventory and condition data. The Route Strategy teams rely on this to justify maintenance spend. However, data gaps in drainage and geotechnical assets (earthworks) mean that the 'Condition' scores in the strategies often rely on Pavements (HAPMS legacy) as a proxy for overall asset health, distorting the risk profile.
  • National Traffic Information Service (NTIS): The central nervous system of the SRN. Processes data from MIDAS and floating vehicle data to feed the outcome: Journey Time Reliability. A legacy monolith currently undergoing painful transformation (NTIS V3), creating data latency issues for RCCs.

Currently, this data is siloed and retroactive, not predictive.
The strategic data lake initiative intended to replace the legacy HAPMS.
It aims to unify asset data (pavement, structures, geotech).
Currently in a tension-filled implementation phase where legacy data quality issues are hindering the 'Digital Twin' vision.
  • HART (Highways Agency Road Traffic) System - Roadside Technology: Middleware abstraction layer intended to decouple central systems from roadside devices. Development creates friction with the NRTS (National Roads Telecommunications Services) contract holder (Telent) regarding who owns the API definitions and latency SLAs.
  • HASS (Highways Asset Spatial System): The definitive geospatial inventory for SRN assets. While theoretically the 'single source of truth', it suffers from data latency issues during the handover from Major Projects (like A14 Cambridge) to Operations. Critical dependency for generating accurate deterioration models.
The definitive record of what NH owns (geospatial inventory).
It is critical for the A66 and A428 schemes to handover accurate data.
However, there is a sync lag between HASS and the operational maintenance systems (Confirm/Ellipse), meaning RCCs sometimes don't know the precise configuration of a newly upgraded junction.
  • HAPMS (Highways Agency Pavement Management System): The legacy monolithic 'system of record' for pavement data. Despite the 'Digital Roads' vision, this 20+ year old Oracle-based system still drives the logic for billion-pound renewal decisions. It calculates the Condition PI. It is a major blocker for real-time digital twin aspirations due to rigid schema structures.
Legacy system of record for pavement condition data (TRACS/SCANNER).
It is technically obsolete and hinders predictive maintenance modelling, creating a 'data debt' friction point for the M25 reconstruction team who rely on it for volumetric scoping.
Legacy system representing a major technical debt.
It holds the pavement data required to justify RIS3 renewal funds.
Migration to the new IAM-IS (Integrated Asset Management) is lagging, meaning RIS3 evidence is partly based on fragmented spreadsheets and HAPMS extracts.
System of Record for pavement condition data (TRACS).
Essential for modeling long-term renewals investment for RIS3 planning but currently suffering from data fragmentation issues.
Legacy system (transitioning to IAM IS) for managing pavement condition data derived from TRACS and SCANNER surveys.
Used to model deterioration and plan resurfacing interventions within the RIS funding cycles.
The repository and analysis tool for pavement data, used to model deterioration and inform the Pavement Logic mapping for planned renewals (often transitioning functionalities to HAMS/IAM IS).
Legacy system (transitioning to IAM-IS) used for storing pavement construction history, condition data (TRACS), and generating SCRIM coefficients.
The system of record for SRN pavement inventory and condition data.
It stores historical survey data, construction history, and supports the modelling of pavement deterioration.
  • GDMS (Geotechnical Data Management System): Stores data on earthworks, slopes, and embankments. Critical for managing landslide risks (e.g., A66). Historically siloed from HAPMS, meaning pavement renewals often happen without awareness that the embankment underneath is failing.
Specialised application for managing geotechnical assets (earthworks, slopes, retaining walls).
It supports compliance with DMRB standard CS 641, tracking slope stability risks and informing geotechnical maintenance allocations.
The repository for geotechnical asset data, managing earthworks, slopes, and retaining walls.
Supports compliance with DMRB standard CD 622.
Critical for managing risks related to landslides and severe weather resilience.
The specialised application for managing geotechnical asset data (earthworks, slopes, embankments), supporting CS 641 (Managing the maintenance of highway geotechnical assets).
  • dTIMS Pavement Modelling Engine: The deterministic deterioration modelling engine used to predict pavement lifecycles across the SRN. It consumes SCANNER and TRACS data to output 20-year condition profiles. Operational reality: The model's calibration often diverges from regional engineering assessments (e.g., in Area 9), leading to 'computer says replace' vs. 'engineer says patch' conflicts. It struggles to accurately model the rapid failure curves of older Thin Surface Course Systems (TSCS) compared to Hot Rolled Asphalt.
  • HART (Highways Asset Resilience and Telemetry): The target state cloud-native platform replacing parts of NTIS. Currently in partial delivery for RIS3, focusing on uncoupling hardware operational status from traffic flow logic. It introduces an Event-Driven Architecture to ingest high-frequency sensor data from tunnels (e.g., A3 Hindhead) and smart motorways. Operational friction exists where HART data models clash with legacy DATEX II export structures required by third-party aggregators.
The target state Operational Technology platform intended to replace the fragmented COBS and HALOGEN landscape.
Currently in transitional deployment.
It aims to unify asset condition data (from inspections) with real-time operational status, but data migration from legacy YAML files is proving technically debt-heavy.
  • SMIS (Structures Management Information System): The master repository for the SRN's 20,000+ structures (bridges, gantries, retaining walls). Calculates the Bridge Condition Index (BCI) based on General and Principal Inspections (GI/PI) mandated by DMRB CS 450. Critical tension: It is a legacy relational database that creates a silo between pavement and structures planning, complicating the alignment of closures for cross-asset renewals (e.g., waterproofing a bridge deck while resurfacing the M6 J13-15).
The definitive register for 20,000+ bridges and structures.
Unlike pavement data, structures data relies heavily on manual General Inspections (GI) and Principal Inspections (PI).
Data latency can be up to 2 years between inspection and system entry, risking 'surprise' failures like the A52 Clifton Bridge closure.
The definitive database for bridge and structure assets on the SRN.
It records General and Principal Inspection (GI/PI) results, BCI (Bridge Condition Indices), and load carrying capacities, essential for maintaining CS 450 compliance.
The definitive database for SRN bridges, tunnels, and gantries.
Stores General Inspection and Principal Inspection records, calculating Bridge Condition Indices (BCI).
Supports compliance with DMRB CS 450 (Inspection of Highway Structures).
The definitive database for the inventory and condition of bridges, tunnels, retaining walls, and gantries on the SRN.
  • HADDMS (Highways Agency Drainage Data Management System): The definitive, yet perpetually struggling, repository for drainage asset inventory and condition data. It anchors the transition from cyclical to risk-based maintenance but suffers from historical data gaps (Legacy 'Grade 4' data). Crucial for generating the Mandated Drainage Maintenance schedules for M&R contractors.
The definitive asset register for drainage and outfalls.
Critical for managing run-off pollution into watercourses (DMRB LA 113).
Currently suffers from data quality issues where historical 'orphan' assets from the A-road network are unmapped, creating liability risks under the Water Framework Directive.
The legacy system of record for drainage assets.
Contains significant data quality gaps regarding asset condition and connectivity, specifically for culverts under the A1 and M1.
This lack of accurate data prevents precise hydraulic modeling for extreme precipitation events, forcing reliance on anecdotal 'flooding hotspot' lists.
  • PINS Infrastructure Planning Portal: External system hosting the Examination Library. NH teams must scrape/monitor this daily during Examination for 'Rule 6' letters and Interested Party representations. Lack of API integration creates manual overhead.
  • National Traffic Information Service (NTIS) Legacy Platform: The current 'burning platform'. Provides the traffic data feed to sat-navs and variable message signs (VMS). It is commercially constrained by legacy contracts, limiting our ability to innovate with real-time connected vehicle data. It feeds the NTIM (National Traffic Information Model).
The backbone of the SRN's situational awareness, feeding the Traffic England website and sat-nav providers.
It represents a significant 'Assurance Gap'.
While Major Projects are heavily audited, this aging logic-monolith (processing MIDAS loop data) receives insufficient technical debt assurance despite being critical for the 97% network availability KPI.
The aging heartbeat of the SRN.
Collects real-time traffic data from MIDAS loops and ANPR.
Currently a massive constraint on digital transformation due to proprietary interfaces (DATEX II v2.3) and high technical debt.
While the HART programme aims to replace it, NTIS still drives the control room walls at NTOC and RCCs.
If this fails, we lose visibility of the network.
The aging 'brain' of the network.
Aggregates data from MIDAS and ANPR.
Heavily constrained by 15-year-old architectural decisions.
Cannot ingest real-time connected vehicle data at scale without crashing the Datex II operational feed to broadcasters.
The primary bottleneck for Digital Roads vision.
The monolithic 'Network Model' engine located primarily at Quinton (with DR at Godstone).
It aggregates telemetry from 14,000+ MIDAS loops, ANPR cameras, and increasingly Floating Vehicle Data (FVD).
It is the 'single source of truth' for the SRN status, but suffers from significant technical debt.
It feeds the Traffic England website and the NVRM (National Variable Response Manager) for setting VMS signals.
Critically, it is the operational bottleneck for 'Digital Roads' transformation due to its tightly coupled architecture which complicates the migration to cloud-native microservices.
  • Citizen Space / Consultation Hub: The digital platform used to host consultation materials and ingest responses. A friction point exists here: the system structure often forces 'structured' data (radio buttons) while stakeholders want to submit unstructured 'free text' objections. Integration with backend analysis tools (Analyze, Nvivo) is often manual and error-prone.
  • HART (Highway Applications and Remote Traffic): The strategic replacement for legacy traffic management systems. Currently in a complex transitional phase. This represents the shift from 'monitoring traffic' to 'active traffic management' and digital twins, but integration with legacy MIDAS loops is proving technically debt-heavy.
The new cloud-native operational platform replacing legacy command and control systems.
It acts as the central nervous system for Traffic Officers and Control Room Operators.
Operational reality: Currently running in parallel with legacy stacks creating data synchronization friction.
Critical for enabling future Digital Roads initiatives but constrained by dependence on legacy roadside operational technology.
The new cloud-native data platform replacing legacy warehousing.
Critical for CAVs because legacy NTIS (National Traffic Information Service) has too high latency (minutes) for safety-critical V2X messaging (milliseconds).
HART is the architectural bridge to expose BCI (Bridge Condition Index) and TRads data to insurers.
The emerging cloud-native data platform intended to replace legacy reporting.

The modern replacement/overlay for legacy reporting tools.

  • IAM IS (Integrated Asset Management Information System): The system of record for pavement and structures. It holds the 'static' twin data (inventory). It is historically disconnected from operations, meaning Control Centres often lack real-time visibility of asset condition (e.g., barrier damage) until inspected.
The target repository for ADMM data, replacing legacy silos (HAPMS, SMIS).

The central register replacing legacy SMIS (Structures Management Information System).

  • Network Occupancy Management System (NOMS): The operational chokepoint. Suppliers must book road space here. It feeds into the Network management dashboard. The primary road space booking system used by supply chain and internal operational teams to schedule access (TSRGD-compliant traffic management).

Architectural weakness: The system incentivises 'ghost bookings'—contractors booking excess capacity 'just in case'—which artificially depresses predicted availability figures unless manually purged.
  • HART (Highways Analyst and Reporting Tool): Used by NH Intelligence Units to verify supplier claims about journey time reliability during roadworks. If a supplier says 'no delays caused' but HART shows a 15-minute spike, the CPF score is manually adjusted downwards.

  • Collaborative Performance Framework (CPF): Internal NH system where supplier performance scores are recorded. Social Value scores from SVP are manually keyed into CPF, introducing human error risk and lagging indicators that don't reflect real-time site reality.
The digital toolkit used to record and visualise supplier performance scores across the Strategic Road Network (SRN) supply chain.
It aggregates data to support the Supplier Incentive Mechanisms (SIM) and strategic dialogue with Tier 1 partners.
  • BRAVO Solutions (Jaggaer) / Atamis: The legacy e-sourcing and contract management platform. It creates a data silo where contract variations are stored but not easily integrated with the Project Control Framework (PCF) or financial systems (Oracle), leading to visibility gaps on committed spend.
  • CEMAR (Contract Management System): The SaaS platform holding the 'single source of truth' for NEC4 contract administration (Early Warnings, Compensation Events). While it manages the workflow, it fails to integrate seamlessly with the Oracle financial ledger, necessitating manual 'swivel chair' data entry for actual payments, increasing error risk.
The SaaS platform (ThinkProject) where the 'war' happens.
All Early Warning Notices (EWN), Compensation Events (CE), and Project Manager Instructions (PMI) are logged here.
It is the single source of truth for commercial liability, distinct from the engineering reality in the Common Data Environment (CDE).
  • HART (Highways Asset Risk Tool): The target system for residual risk data from the H&S File. Used by Operations to plan maintenance. If CDM data isn't structured to map to HART taxonomies, manual workarounds are required, increasing the risk of unawareness during emergency repairs.
  • AIRSWeb Safety Management System: The primary platform for recording accidents and 'near misses'. While it captures acute injuries well, it struggles to effectively track chronic occupational health latencies like noise-induced hearing loss.
  • Esri ArcGIS Enterprise: The corporate GIS platform. Provides the geospatial view of the SRN. Integration with the asset database (IAM IS) is the biggest architectural headache we have right now.
  • HART (Highways Agency Road Network Topology): The master linear referencing system. It defines where 'M6 J19' actually is. If HART data is stale, the Control Centres (RCCs) send Traffic Officers to the wrong location.
  • Social Value Portal (SVP): Third-party SaaS platform used to track TOMs. It is NOT integrated with the National Highways Common Data Environment (CDE) or HART, creating a data silo where social value data exists separately from operational project controls.
  • HART (Highway Awareness, Restoration and Traffic): The target state data platform intended to replace legacy traffic systems. Currently in a complex transitional phase where it must ingest data from legacy loops while trying to integrate Connected Vehicle data. The coupling between HART and the actual roadside operational technology is currently fragile.
  • EnvIS (Environmental Information System): The central repository for environmental data (noise barriers, cultural heritage, landscape). Technically the 'single source of truth', but in reality, data from major schemes (A428, A66) is often bulk-uploaded late in the delivery phase (Stage 6), meaning Operations has zero visibility of new environmental assets until handover.
The central repository for environmental asset data.
In reality, it is a data graveyard.
Consultants dump GIS shapefiles here post-construction, but Operations rarely access it to maintain the assets (e.g., oil separators) effectively, leading to compliance drift.
Legacy system of record for National Highways environmental data.
Currently constitutes a significant technical debt; it struggles to ingest complex Defra Metric 4.0 spatial data structures, creating a 'digital gap' where BNG calculations live in disconnected Excel sheets rather than the enterprise architecture.
The specific National Highways system of record for environmental assets and data.
Stores inventory of noise barriers, cultural heritage sites, and landscape elements.
Essential for generating environmental asset management plans (EAMPs) and reporting against RIS performance metrics.
  • Oracle HCM Cloud: Human Capital Management. Critical for tracking Traffic Officer (TO) certifications and safety passports. If this drifts from reality, we risk deploying uncertified staff to live lanes.
The primary System of Record for employee data.
While functionally rich, its rigid workflows often clash with the dynamic nature of regional operations and incident response rostering, leading to 'shadow HR' spreadsheets in regional depots.
  • Bentley ProjectWise: The 'Source of Truth' for engineering data (ECM). It holds the DCO application documents for Lower Thames Crossing and A303 Stonehenge. If the CAD file isn't here, the bridge doesn't exist legally.
  • Microsoft Power BI Corporate Reporting: The visualization layer that aggregates LARS (Lane Availability) and KPI metrics for the DfT. It often masks the data quality issues lurking in the underlying source systems.
  • National Traffic Information Service (NTIS) Network Model: The central operational brain. It ingests data from MIDAS loops and Floating Vehicle Data (FVD) to calculate journey times. It is currently a legacy constraint; while it feeds sat-navs and VMS, its update cycle is too slow for the immediate demands of Connected and Autonomous Vehicle (CAV) trials defined in RIS3.
  • COBS (Control Office Base System): The legacy signalling control system used in RCCs to set speeds and red X signals on Smart Motorways. It is a critical dependency that is difficult to patch without requiring network downtime. It interfaces directly with roadside outstations via aged copper and fibre lines.
The specialized application component responsible for the interface between the control centre and roadside technology.
It translates operator commands into specific protocols to control Variable Message Signs (VMS), Advanced Motorway Indicators (AMI), and collect data from MIDAS outstations.
  • CHARM / DYNAC Traffic Management System: The Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) used in Regional Control Centres. There is a critical architectural coupling here: HART must deliver telemetry to CHARM with sub-second latency to ensure that when a Traffic Officer sets a 'Red X', it actually appears on the gantry. Recent software integration issues between the HART IP stream and the DYNAC controllers have caused programme delays.
The central Advanced Traffic Management System (Advanced Traffic Management System).
It acts as the source of truth for setting VMS signs.
We are struggling to expose CHARM data via API to the C-ITS cloud fast enough to match the visual signs, creating a dangerous 'latency gap' where the dashboard disagrees with the gantry.
The Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) used by RCCs to control roadside technology.
It interfaces with roadside outstations to set VMS text, speed limits, and lane closures (Red X).
Replacing the legacy HART system as part of the operational technology roadmap.
The operational interface used by ROC operators to set signals and monitor events (transitioning from legacy systems to a unified Advanced Traffic Management System).
  • NH Azure Data Lake (Raw Ingestion Layer): The 'Swamp'. Ingests raw telemetry from HALOGEN (incident logs), CHARM (traffic management), and SCANNER (pavement condition). Contains vast amounts of unstructured CCTV metadata and uncleaned MIDAS loop data. Critical for data scientists but dangerous for business reporting due to lack of schema enforcement and data quality controls.
  • Enterprise Data Warehouse (Curated Layer): Structured SQL environment (Snowflake/Synapse) where raw lake data is modelled into 'Gold' standard datasets for RIS reporting. This is where the 'One Version of the Truth' fights happen—reconciling P50 Availability figures between Operations and Strategy directorates. Feeds the ORR performance monitor reports.
  • Asset Deterioration Modelling Engine (dTIMS/Python): Predictive analytics engine using machine learning to forecast pavement and structure degradation. It ingests HAPMS and IAM-IS data to generate the 'Forward Works Programme'. There is significant tension here: the model often suggests renewals that Regional Delivery Partnerships (RDPs) cannot deliver within the RIS2 funding envelope due to inflation.
  • PowerBI Corporate Performance Dashboard: The executive visualization layer used by the Board and DfT. Displays KPI metrics like 'Killed or Seriously Injured' (KSI) reductions and 'Customer Service Score'. Often masks the underlying data quality issues in the source systems (HALOGEN) regarding incident classification.
  • ESDAL (Electronic Service Delivery for Abnormal Loads): Legacy monolith used by hauliers to plot Abnormal Indivisible Load (AIL) routes. A major friction point: the interface is antiquated, causing high manual processing overhead for Structure owners to approve bridge crossings. Acts as a constraint on the 'Digital Roads' vision due to hard-coded logic regarding structural weight limits and lack of integration with the modern geospatial asset register (IAM).
A web-based portal allowing hauliers to plot routes and notify police and bridge authorities.
It integrates with National Highways structure data to automatically check route viability against bridge weight limits.
  • Street Manager (DfT Central Service): External SaaS platform mandated by DfT for lane rental and roadworks permitting. NH must integrate with this despite it being designed primarily for Local Authorities. Creates an architectural boundary issue where NH data (from Schedule of Roadworks) must flow into a system we do not control to coordinate with utility companies.
  • Local Tunnel SCADA (PLC Logic): The operational brain: Siemens or similar PLC logic handling real-time matrix, ventilation, and barrier interlocks. Operates independently of national systems (HART/NTIS) to ensure fail-safe operation. A major legacy constraint; upgrading this requires full tunnel closures, clashing with P50 availability targets.
  • Legacy Tunnel SCADA Systems: Fragmented operational technology estate. Many tunnel PLCs are effectively 'black boxes' that do not expose API data to the National Traffic Information Service (NTIS). Maintenance relies on specialist contractors rather than standard TS operational teams.
  • Tunnel Control System (SCADA) - Hindhead Local Node: Local operational technology (OT) controlling fans, lighting, and barriers. Represents a legacy 'island of automation' that does not fully integrate with the national HART (Highways Agency Road Traffic) system, causing data silos.
  • MIDAS (Motorway Incident Detection and Automatic Signalling): Queue protection system on tunnel approaches. Vital for preventing secondary collisions (which account for 20% of casualties) when the tunnel suddenly closes.
Legacy induction loop and radar system embedded in the carriageway.
Provides HIOCC (High Occupancy) alerts for queue protection.
Currently faces obsolescence challenges and maintenance access issues on busy ALR sections.
A distributed system of inductive loops and radar sensors that detects traffic flow and queueing.
It automatically triggers 'Queue Caution' signals and feeds data into control room systems for congestion analysis.
  • Legacy Tunnel SCADA System (Modbus/PLC): Disparate Operational Technology (OT) layer across older tunnels. Often runs on out-of-support Windows versions or aging PLC hardware. Creates a 'digital air gap' where real-time asset condition data (fan vibration, CO levels) cannot easily feed into national systems like HART or IPM (Integrated Planned Maintenance), preventing predictive maintenance.
  • A3 Hindhead Tunnel SCADA Master System: Primary Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition assembly (WinCC OA based) for the A3 Hindhead tunnels. Orchestrates sub-systems (ventilation, lighting, linear heat detection) and provides the HMI for RCC Godstone. High operational friction due to proprietary protocols preventing easy integration with the modern HART data lake initiatives. Criticality: P1.
  • Tunnel Video Management System (MIST Protocol): CCTV aggregation layer. Uses the legacy MIST protocol (unlike the ONVIF standards pushed by Digital D&D). This forces a complex translation layer to get video feeds into the National Traffic Operations Centre (NTOC) video wall, causing 3-5 seconds of latency which is borderline acceptable for incident management.
  • Tunnel SCADA & Ventilation Control System: Legacy Operational Technology (OT) controlling jet fans and extractors. In a HAZMAT incident, this system must switch ventilation strategies (longitudinal vs. transverse) instantly. Integration with the newer CHARM/HART platform remains a complex architectural debt item, creating a 'swivel-chair' interface for operators.
  • Tunnel Facility Management System (Legacy SCADA): On-premise control software. Lacks cybersecurity patching compliance for modern standards (TS 50701). Data silo that does not feed real-time asset condition to the National Traffic Information Service (NTIS), blinding the National Network Manager to granular tunnel availability risks.
  • CHARM / ATMS (Advanced Traffic Management System): The National Control Centre system that must ingest V2X data (stopped vehicle alerts, pothole detection). Currently struggling to integrate high-frequency probe data from connected vehicles without overwhelming the operator interface in the RCCs.

The Collaborative Highways Agency Response Management system.
The core operational application used in Regional Control Centres (RCCs) and the National Network Management Centre (NNMC) to set signals, monitor incidents, and control smart motorway infrastructure.
The outcome of the Charm programme (Collaborative Highways for Advanced Road Management), replacing legacy HART and instation systems.
It provides the unified interface for RCC operators to set signals, manage VMS, and log incidents.
  • HART (Highway Applications and Remote Tolling): Legacy command and control system used in RCCs. Monolithic architecture that is difficult to update. Impedes the integration of modern, API-driven data sources from Connected Vehicles.
  • HART (Highway Audit and Readiness Tool): The critical digital system mapping the SRN's 'readability' for AVs. Currently a strategic prototype, but the Law Commission's recall powers imply HART must become a safety-critical system (SCS) to warn ASDEs of infrastructure degradation (e.g., faded white lines).
  • CHARM (Common Highways Agency Rijkswaterstaat Model): The delayed 'savior' system intended to replace HART. Deployment has been fraught with integration complexities between standard IT protocols and non-standard roadside OT (legacy serial connections). The tension between 'configuration' (Standard) and 'customisation' (NH Specifics) has blown budgets and timelines.
The perpetually delayed next-gen traffic management system intended to replace HART.
Meant to harmonize operations between England and the Netherlands.
Its deployment delays enforce reliance on legacy technology, stalling the Modernising Operational Systems (MOS) programme.
The new Advanced Traffic Management System deployed in RCCs (e.g., Godstone, Wakefield).
It replaces legacy operational interfaces but has suffered significant integration delays with existing roadside technology.
The delayed successor to HART (based on Kapsch traffic management).
Currently running in parallel/shadow mode in specific regions.
Its integration with legacy roadside technology remains a major architectural friction point.
Implied endpoint for TriggeringRelationship to CHARM (Common Highways Agency Rijkswaterstaat Model)
The new Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) replacing legacy regional systems.
It consolidates control room functions across ROCCs, enabling cross-boundary incident management and supporting future connected vehicle standards.
Next-generation Advanced Traffic Management System intended to replace legacy COBS/HALOGEN systems in ROCs.
Deployment has faced significant integration challenges and delays, creating a hybrid operational technology landscape.
The Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) used in Regional Control Centres (RCCs) to monitor and control the Strategic Road Network (SRN).
It replaces legacy systems (COBS) to manage Smart Motorways, variable speed limits, and lane closures, supporting RIS2 safety outcomes.
The advanced traffic management system (ATMS) based on Kapsch DYNAC software.
Deployed in Regional Control Centres (RCCs), it enables operators to set signals (AMI/MS4) on Smart Motorways, manage incidents, and coordinate responses, replacing legacy COBS systems.
The Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) used in RCCs to monitor the network, control electronic signals/signs, and manage incident workflows, replacing legacy operational systems.
  • ProjectWise / Asite (Federated CDE): The Common Data Environments (CDE) used by the supply chain (e.g., Skanska, Balfour Beatty) to host the Project Information Model (PIM). Critical architectural flaw: NH does not own the native CDE for every scheme; we often only receive the exports, losing the rich metadata context and audit trails contained in the contractor's proprietary environment.
  • Traffic England (Web & Public Service Wrapper): The public-facing digital front-end for SRN status. While visibly the primary channel for the public, it suffers from technical debt and architectural coupling to the legacy NTIS Model 1 architecture. It struggles to compete with the latency and UI/UX of Google/Waze but remains the 'single source of truth' for statutory closure data and confirmed incidents (verified by NTOC). Displays feed from MIDAS and CCTV, subject to filtering for privacy (GDPR) and suicide prevention protocols.
  • HART (Highways Agency Road Traffic) Platform: Cloud-native replacement initiative for legacy traffic data systems. Currently running in parallel with NTIS. The tension lies in the migration strategy: we are maintaining dual costs for cloud ingress/egress while legacy operational apps (COBS) refuse to decouple from the old NTIS operational database.
  • Tunnel Facility Management System (SCADA/PLC): The operational technology controlling ventilation, lighting, and drainage. In older assets, this is often running on legacy OS (Windows 7/XP) with air-gapped security. There is a critical dependency here: modernizing these systems for cyber-compliance often requires long-duration closures that destroy Network Availability metrics (P50), leading to deferral of upgrades.
  • CHARM (Collaborative Traffic Management System): The Advanced Traffic Management System deployed at Regional Control Centres (e.g., Godstone, Quinton). It replaces legacy COBS. Integration with the new SVD (Stopped Vehicle Detection) radar has been operationally painful, causing high false alarm rates that frustrate Traffic Officers and skew LARS (Lane Availability Reporting System) metrics.
  • Oracle Fusion HCM: The primary ERP system of record for workforce data. Currently acts as a constraint on agility due to poor integration with operational rostering systems used in RCCs, creating a 'data gap' between theoretical headcount and actual shift availability for incident response.
  • Oracle E-Business Suite (EBS): Our legacy ERP backbone. It is a significant constraint on digital transformation. While we have fancy front-end dashboards, the core ledgers are rigid. Integrating real-time asset costs from IAM IS (Asset Management) into Oracle for accurate Whole Life Costing is a manual, friction-heavy nightmare.
The monolithic legacy ERP.
Handles General Ledger and Accounts Payable.
It forces a 'capitalisation' logic that makes tracking operational expenditure (OpEx) on Smart Motorway technology refreshes painful.
The current, highly customised on-premise ERP handling general ledger, AP/AR, and procurement.
It is end-of-life and heavily modified to support the 'Scheme Accounting' logic used for the Roads Investment Strategy (RIS).
It currently creates a data silo that disconnects financial actuals from the project performance data in the miserable Excel spreadsheets used by Commercial Directors.
  • Claims Management & Recovery System: The legacy case management database used by the Green and Red claims teams. It lacks real-time integration with the Command and Control system (control works) or HART, requiring manual data scraping from incident logs to prove liability. This 'swivel-chair' integration is a major leakage point for cost recovery.
  • Salesforce CRM (Stakeholder Engagement): The central repository for tracking interactions with landowners, MPs, and local authorities. It is heavily customized and often poorly integrated with the Correspondence Tracking System (CTS), leading to data silos where regional project teams (e.g., A428 delivery) may not be aware of previous commitments made by the Public Affairs team to local MPs.
  • HART Legacy Command & Control System: Ageing operational technology used in Regional Control Centres. Represents a massive unmitigated technical debt risk. If HART fails, manual contingency (traffic officers on patrol) cannot maintain safe SRN operations, yet replacement is consistently deferred for 'value engineering'.
  • Building Management System (BMS): Centralized control of HVAC, lighting, and access control across the estate. Currently fragmented across regions; lack of a unified 'Digital Twin' for the estate prevents predictive maintenance, leading to reactive failures in control room cooling systems.
  • Total Resource Management (TRM) System: The rostering engine for Traffic Officers and RCC staff. It determines who is on the road. The legacy system has poor integration with the Oracle HR record, leading to payroll errors for shift allowances—a massive dissatisfier for frontline staff that the People Strategy must resolve to prevent union action.
  • AIRSWeb (Safety Reporting System): Legacy system of record for all incidents (accident, near miss, abuse). UX friction often leads to under-reporting of 'low level' hazards by supply chain, skewing the Accident Frequency Rate (AFR) data used for executive reporting.
  • Nochex / Network Occupancy Management System: The system used to book road space. The clash point: Maintenance contractors, Major Projects, and Utilities all fighting for the same stretch of the M1. Conflicts are often resolved by 'he who shouts loudest' rather than strategic optimization.
  • CHARM (Dynac) Advanced Traffic Management System: The primary operational interface replacing legacy COBS. Controls signals, variable speed limits, and receives MIDAS/SVD alerts. Deployment was delayed; currently creates friction where legacy COBS protocols clash with Dynac's object-oriented logic. Specific reliance for Smart Motorway signaling.
  • AIRS (Accident and Incident Reporting System): Legacy internal system for recording RIDDOR events, staff injuries, and asset damage. While it captures the 'what', it struggles to capture the unstructured 'why' or root cause analysis effectively for wider dissemination.
  • HART (Highways Action Response Tool): The replacement for the legacy HALOGEN/COBRAS stack. A cloud-native operational control system. Currently creating operational friction as veteran operators struggle with UI latency compared to the instant response of legacy command-line tools. Critical dependency for managing Smart Motorway signals and variable speed limits.
The primary operational logging and dispatch system replacing legacy Command & Control functionality, used to manage incidents and record timelines for performance reporting.
  • Dart Charge Payment System: The primary 'User Pays' revenue collection engine on the SRN. It is not just a billing system; it is a critical demand management tool for the Dartford Crossing. Failure here causes immediate tailbacks onto the M25 (Safety Critical). Recently transitioned vendors, highlighting the fragility of legacy tolling data migration.
  • Bravo (Jaggaer) eSourcing: The procurement front-end used by Commercial to tender packages. A legacy constraint; it creates a data silo where tender pricing data sits, often disconnected from the actual out-turn cost data in CEMAR, making 'Should Cost' modelling for future RIS periods difficult.
  • HART (Highways Agency Road Traffic) - Highways Asset Risk Tool (HART): The strategic asset management system replacing HAPMS; designed to predict failure (potholes, flooding) using decay modelling; adoption is hindered by poor quality historic data (LARS/SCANNER) migration.
  • WebDris / DAS (Departures Approval System): The repository of engineering concessions. It represents a massive, largely untapped dataset of where the DMRB is failing to meet modern delivery constraints or innovation needs.
The legacy operational system used to log, track, and approve departures from DMRB.
It is a critical data silo that contains the record of all accepted risks on the network, but is poorly integrated with the newer IPM (Integrated Project Management) platform and GDMS (Geotechnical Data Management System).
  • IAM (Integrated Asset Management) / HAPMS: The system of record for pavement and structures. Currently transitioning from HAPMS to the new IAM stack. Data quality is poor; regional teams often keep 'shadow spreadsheets' of asset condition because they don't trust the central LARS/SCANNER data ingest.
  • Asset Management System (IAM): The repository of truth for SRN assets. It is cluttered with poor quality historical data (legacy HAPMS imports). AI predictive maintenance initiatives fail here because the training data for pavement degradation is inconsistent across different Areas (e.g., Area 9 vs Area 10 data standards differ).
The master asset register (based on confirm/statutory data).
It contains significant data gaps ('unknown' condition scores) for legacy drainage and geotechnical assets, making risk-based funding allocation for RIS3 highly speculative.
  • HART (Highways Agency Road Traffic) Core System: The legacy operational Command & Control (C&C) system deployed locally across Regional Control Centres (RCCs) such as Godstone, South Mimms, and Wakefield. While ostensibly being superseded by the CHARM program, HART remains the 'fingers-on-glass' reality for Traffic Officers setting signals on the SRN. It creates the critical abstraction layer between the operator and the HALOGEN subsystem to drive AMI (Advanced Motorway Indicators) and MS4 signs. Critical tension: It is a legacy monolith that struggles to support modern RIS2 Connected Corridor initiatives without significant middleware wrappers.
The absolute bedrock legacy system for historical traffic data.
Despite being archaic, Route Strategies depend on HART data to prove congestion hotspots (Delay > 10s/vehicle/km).
The lack of granular integration with newer HATRIS analysis tools creates significant manual overhead during the evidence phase.

Legacy monitoring and signal setting components still operational in specific regions or functional silos, interfacing with the wider Control Office System (COS) network alongside newer CHARM deployments.
  • HALOGEN Subsystem: The protocol handler within the HART ecosystem that translates high-level operator commands into the low-level TR2513 protocols required by roadside outstations. It manages the 'aspect sequences' to ensure compliance with TSRGD (Traffic Signs Regulations and General Directions). It represents a major constraint in digital transformation; you cannot simply 'upgrade' the front end without risking the integrity of these safety-critical signal instructions.
  • HART (Highways Accident and Reporting Tool): SaaS-based enterprise EHS platform serving as the single source of truth for GG 128 incident reporting across National Highways and the Tier 1 supply chain. Unlike operational control systems (NTIS/CHARM), HART focuses on governance, compliance, and 'Home Safe and Well' strategic outcomes. It captures personal injury, asset damage, and near-miss data from schemes like A428 Black Cat and Lower Thames Crossing. It is currently a legacy constraint, with significant friction caused by lack of API integration with supply chain partner systems, necessitating manual double-keying of safety data.
The cloud-native replacement for the legacy Command & Control system.
Critical path for ingesting future CAV data streams.
Currently constrained by the need to support legacy MIDAS loop inputs while architecting for high-volume floating vehicle data (FVD).
  • CEMAR (NEC4 Contract Management): The *de facto* record of truth for compensation events (CEs) and early warnings (EWNs) across Major Projects. While it digitalises contract administration, it often becomes a weaponised audit trail rather than a collaboration tool, with data siloed away from the Enterprise Data Warehouse.
  • JAGGAER (BravoSolution): The eSourcing platform used for tendering. Legacy architecture that creates significant friction for SMEs trying to bid for work. Data structure here rarely aligns with the PCF (Project Control Framework) stages, causing disconnects between 'what was bought' and 'what is being built'.
  • Lane Availability Reporting System (LARS): The definitive reporting engine for RIS2/RIS3 Network Availability KPI calculations. It aggregates planned closures from NOMS against confirmed activations from NTIS. Critically, LARS is a post-event reporting tool, not real-time; it creates a 'lag' between operational reality and regulatory reporting, often requiring manual data cleansing by regional teams to resolve discrepancies where 'Booked' does not equal 'Closed'.
  • SVD Radar System: Infrastructure-side radar (typically Navtech ClearWay) deployed on Smart Motorways. Scans carriageway 360-degrees to detect stationary objects. Interfaces directly with the instation to generate high-priority alarms for ROC operators.
  • HALOGEN: Legacy Command & Control system used in many RCCs. Being progressively decommissioned. Logs incident details and manages Traffic Officer dispatch. High technical debt; limited integration with modern V2X data streams compared to its successor, CHARM.
The winter fleet management system used to track gritters and salt usage.
Essential for maintaining network availability during severe weather events (SWAD), ensuring compliance with winter maintenance standards.
  • CHARM (Collaborative Highways for Active Reliable Mobility): Next-generation Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) based on the specific Kapsch Dynac platform. Centralizes control logic, replacing HALOGEN and diverse instations. Critical for future Digital Roads vision and unified incident handling.
  • IAM (Integrated Asset Management System): The core repository for asset inventory and condition data (formerly HAPMS). Stores critical data on pavement quality (SCRIM), drainage, and geotechnical assets to inform decision-support tools for renewal planning.
  • Command & Control (Airwave/ESN): Mission-critical communication system used by Traffic Officers (TOs) and Control Rooms to coordinate with emergency services (Police/Ambulance) under JESIP principles.
  • CHARM (Collaborative Highways Agency Response Management): The primary operational platform used in Regional Control Centres (RCCs) to manage incidents. CHARM interfaces with roadside technology (signals, VMS) to set Red X and variable speed limits (Smart Motorways), replacing legacy COBS systems.
The Advanced Traffic Management System (ATMS) deployed at Regional Control Centres (RCCs).
It serves as the primary interface for Traffic Officers to monitor the network, manage incidents, and control roadside electronic signage (VMS/AMI) on Smart Motorways.
Replaces legacy Command and Control systems.
  • NOMS (Network Occupancy Management System): The scheduling application used to book road space on the SRN. It creates the Schedule of Road Works (SRW) and prevents spatial/temporal conflicts between maintenance delivery partners and major project delivery teams.
The tactical system used to book and manage road space access on the SRN.
It ensures co-ordination between maintenance contractors, major projects (e.g., Lower Thames Crossing), and statutory undertakers to minimize disruption, adhering to NRSWA and TSRGD constraints.
Application used to book road space and coordinate roadworks to prevent conflicts and manage network availability (KPI).
The system of record for booking road space, used by internal maintenance teams and external contractors (Tier 1s) to schedule closures.
  • Airwave Communication Service: The secure TETRA digital radio network application interface used by Traffic Officers and Control Centre operators for mission-critical voice and data communication during incident response, ensuring coordination with emergency services.
  • Traffic England: Public-facing web application and API surface providing real-time traffic information, CCTV imagery, and unplanned event data to road users, supporting the 'Customer Service' performance indicator by enabling informed journey planning.
Public-facing website and API service consuming NTIS data to visualize network status, roadworks, and delays for the public, hauliers, and third-party navigation providers.
  • P2 (Project Control Framework Application): The management information system used to track stage-gate progress (SGARs) of major projects through the Project Control Framework (PCF), ensuring compliance with DfT investment governance.
  • HART (Highways Agency Road Traffic): The core Command and Control system used in Regional Control Centres (RCCs). It provides the central interface for logging incidents, managing event chronologies, integrating map-based visualization of the SRN, and coordinating the response of Traffic Officers and service providers.
Legacy traffic management system still operational in specific regions/functions during the transition to CHARM.
Represents a significant technical debt and integration challenge for the enterprise architecture.
Legacy traffic management application being progressively superseded but still active in specific operational contexts for signal setting and incident logging within Control Centres before full CHARM migration.
  • Command & Control System (Airwave): The secure TETRA radio network and associated dispatch application used for voice communication between RCCs, Traffic Officers, and Emergency Services (JESIP interoperability) during critical incidents.
The critical communication application facilitating secure voice and data dispatch between RCCs and on-road Traffic Officers (TOVs), essential for coordinating emergency responses.
  • Traffic England Digital Service: The public-facing web and API platform that presents real-time traffic information, unplanned disruption alerts, and planned roadworks data to the public, directly supporting the customer service KPI in RIS2.
  • Pellucid: The weather information system aggregating data from roadside Environmental Sensor Stations (ESS) and Met Office feeds. It informs decision-making for winter treatments and high-wind bridge closures (e.g., QEII Bridge, Orwell Bridge).
  • NVRM (National Vehicle Recovery Manager): The system used to manage the statutory removal of broken-down or abandoned vehicles from the SRN, coordinating with recovery operators to clear carriageways and restore capacity (improving Flow Weighted Vehicle Speeds).
  • SVD (Stopped Vehicle Detection) Radar System: Radar-based technology deployed on All Lane Running (ALR) Smart Motorways to detect stationary vehicles in live lanes and alert RCC operators, a key commitment in the Smart Motorways Evidence Stocktake.
  • Stopped Vehicle Detection (SVD) System: Radar-based application layer deployed on All Lane Running (ALR) sections to automatically detect stationary vehicles and alert RCC operators, a critical requirement following the Smart Motorway Evidence Stocktake.
  • Integrated Asset Management (IAM) System: The suite of applications (including Confirm/Ellipse components) used to log Category 1 safety defects (potholes, damaged barriers) found during safety inspections, triggering immediate repair workflows.
  • HAGDMS (Highways Agency Geotechnical Drainage Management System): Critical application for managing drainage assets and flood risks. Holds data on culverts, outfalls, and attenuation ponds. Supports Environmental Mitigation Delivery by ensuring SuDS assets are recorded and maintained to prevent pollution of watercourses (DMRB CG 501).
  • Citizen Space: The digital platform used by National Highways to host consultations and capture stakeholder feedback for major schemes. Central to Community Impact Management, allowing analysis of thousands of responses for projects like the Lower Thames Crossing.
The digital consultation platform used for statutory public consultations on Nationally Significant Infrastructure Projects (NSIPs) and Development Consent Orders (DCOs), such as the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine scheme.
  • ArcGIS Enterprise: Geospatial platform used to model environmental constraints (SSSI, AONB, Ancient Woodland). Used by environmental advisors and supply chain partners to map impacts for Environmental Statements (ES) and Preliminary Environmental Information Reports (PEIR).
  • HART (Highways Apps for Road Tasks): Mobile application suite used by operational staff and contractors to log defects, manage jobs, and record on-site asset data in real-time.
  • NTIS (National Traffic Information Service): System that disseminates road closure information resulting from planned works or reactive incidents to the public and logistics providers.
The system responsible for real-time network visibility and road space booking (Network Occupancy Management System - NOMS integration), ensuring maintenance access does not conflict with major events or other roadworks.
The operational traffic management system that must be updated with new network topology (links and nodes) and technology configurations (MIDAS, VMS) prior to a scheme going live, ensuring accurate traffic data publication and control room visibility.
The central data hub that processes traffic data (MIDAS/FVD) to calculate flow states and disseminate network status to VMS and third parties.
The central nervous system of National Highways, processing real-time data from 10,000+ roadside sensors to generate traffic information.
  • National Collision Database: The central repository (formerly associated with SPOT/MASTR) holding validated collision data for the SRN, allowing engineers to identify cluster sites and calculate benefit-cost ratios for safety schemes.
The central repository used by SES and regional teams to analyze collision trends, supporting the identification of Accident Cluster Sites and contributing to RIS Safety KPIs.
  • CRASH System: Department for Transport (DfT) system used by Police forces to record STATS19 data mobile-first at the scene, which integrates with National Highways' data for analysis.
  • Highways Passport System: A smartcard/digital system for supply chain workforce management, ensuring all workers on SRN sites have valid induction and competency credentials (CSCS) before entry.
  • BravoSolution eSourcing Platform: The official NH e-tendering portal used to manage the full procurement lifecycle, from OJEU/Find a Tender Service (FTS) notices to Pre-Qualification Questionnaires (PQQ) and Invitation to Tender (ITT) for frameworks like the SDF and RDP.
  • CEMAR (Contract Event Management): The cloud-based contract management system mandated for use on National Highways major projects to administer NEC3 and NEC4 contracts. It tracks Compensation Events, Early Warnings, and payment assessments for schemes like the A428 Black Cat to Caxton Gibbet.
  • Echo: The enterprise customer correspondence and complaints management system used to track interactions, FOI requests, and case resolutions, providing data for ORR performance reporting.
  • Traffic Officer Radio Service (TORS): Mission-critical voice communication application operating on the Airwave TETRA network, enabling secure coordination between Traffic Officers, RCCs, and Police.
  • Oracle Primavera P6: The primary Enterprise Project Portfolio Management (EPPM) tool used by National Highways and supply chain to manage critical path schedules for all RIS schemes.
  • PRISM (Project Reporting and Information System for Major Projects): The core performance reporting system for Major Projects, aggregating cost, schedule, and risk data to produce monthly dashboards for the Executive Committee.
  • HAMS (Highways Asset Management System): The core system of record (typically based on Confirm or similar platforms) for asset inventory, condition data, and works ordering. It acts as the 'Single Source of Truth' for asset data as mandated by the Asset Data Management Manual (ADMM).
  • Winter Maintenance Management System: System used to plan gritting routes, monitor spreader vehicle telemetry, and record salt usage for audit purposes.
  • Primavera P6 Enterprise Project Portfolio Management: The standard scheduling and project management software used by National Highways Major Projects to manage the timeline and critical path of RIS schemes.
  • Bentley ProjectWise (CDE): The Common Data Environment (CDE) used for storing and managing design artifacts, CAD drawings, and BIM models across the delivery supply chain.
  • Primavera P6: The enterprise project portfolio management tool used across the Complex Infrastructure Programme (CIP) and Regional Investment Programme (RIP) to manage critical path schedules, resource loading, and Earned Value Management (EVM) reporting for RIS schemes.
  • SVD System (Stopped Vehicle Detection): Radar-based technology deployed on All Lane Running (ALR) smart motorways to automatically detect stationary vehicles and alert the ROC.
  • CEMAR: The cloud-based contract management system used by National Highways and its supply chain to administer NEC3/NEC4 contracts, tracking compensation events, early warnings, and instructions.
  • Departures Approval System (DAS): The workflow system used to submit, review, and approve technical departures from the Design Manual for Roads and Bridges (DMRB).
  • Post Opening Project Evaluation (POPE) System: System/Database used to compare predicted scheme benefits against actual safety and journey time reliability outcomes 1 and 5 years post-opening.

ARCHIMATE:APPLICATIONINTERFACE (1 components):
---------------------------------------------
  • DATEX II Open Data Publication API: The strategic pivot for NH digital strategy. Instead of building better apps, we expose SRN data via ISO 14827 (DATEX II) standards to third-party developers (SatNav providers, logistics firms). This creates a dependency where our operational reputation relies on how accurately third parties interpret our closure data. Critical for meeting DfT 'Open Data' mandates.

ARCHIMATE:APPLICATIONSERVICE (18 components):
-------------------------------------------
  • Virtual Consultation Platform (Citizen Space/Aecom): Digital engagement layer for DCO (Development Consent Order) applications. Critical for schemes like the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine and Lower Thames Crossing. Tensions arise here between 'digital inclusion' requirements and the massive complexity of engineering data presented to the public. Failure here leads to Judicial Review risks.
  • National Traffic Information Service (NTIS): Aggregates live traffic data, incidents and network status for operational decision-making
  • Highways Agency Traffic Information System (HATRIS): Stores historical flow, speed and journey time data for modelling and reporting
  • Regional Operations Control Systems: Control-room systems managing incidents, messaging and lane control
  • National Roads Telecommunications Service (NRTS): Fibre and comms network connecting CCTV, VMS, signals and sensors to operations centres
  • Roadside Communications Platforms: IP-based systems linking smart motorway devices, sensors and control infrastructure
  • Asset Management Information Systems: Platforms storing inspection data, lifecycle plans and asset inventories
  • Works Management Systems: Systems coordinating maintenance schedules, traffic management and contractor activities
  • Infrastructure Data Analytics Platforms: Data environments supporting predictive maintenance and lifecycle modelling
  • Strategic Modelling Platforms: Transport modelling tools used to assess future network scenarios
  • Engineering Information Platforms: Systems storing design models, drawings and digital engineering artefacts
  • Journey Information Distribution Platforms: Disseminate data to signage, feeds, apps and external travel services
  • Public Information Platforms: Systems managing alerts, web updates and public messaging channels
  • Highways Accident Reporting Tool (HART): Corporate system capturing safety events, investigations and corrective actions
  • Environmental Monitoring Systems: Systems collecting and reporting environmental performance indicators
  • Supplier Management Systems: Systems supporting contract oversight, reporting and supplier governance
  • Investment Planning Platforms: Systems supporting RIS planning, portfolio tracking and investment modelling
  • Corporate Reporting Systems: Systems producing dashboards, KPIs and regulatory submissions

  • Asset Condition Assessment (BCI & SCRIM): Data derived from Bridge Condition Index (BCI) and Sideway-force Coefficient Routine Investigation Machine (SCRIM). The deteriorating trend in these metrics indicates a 'maintenance backlog' that is often ignored in favor of shiny new capital projects like LTC, creating a 'time bomb' in the operational architecture.
Bridge Condition Index.
A critical and critical-weighted average score.
Many post-tensioned bridges from the 1970s are deteriorating.
The trade-off is between expensive propping/strengthening works and imposing weight restrictions which harm the economy.
  • Asset Condition: Pavement (LARS/SCANNER): Data derived from TRACS/SCANNER vehicles measuring rutting, texture, and profile. The tension: Data often shows degradation (Amber/Red) requiring intervention, but funding constraints force a 'managed decline' approach on Tier 2/3 roads.
Metrics derived from TRACS and SCANNER surveys.
Used to calculate the Pavement Condition Index (PCI).
A critical trade-off exists here: Strategy teams often prioritize 'visible' pavement defects to satisfy user metrics (Transport Focus), potentially neglecting 'invisible' but critical structural degradation (bridges/concrete cancer) which has higher catastrophic risk.
  • KPI: 60-Minute Incident Clearance: Operational target to clear 85% of incidents within an hour. Tension: Police forensic requirements (Collision Investigation) often override this target, yet the penalty sits with National Highways in the ORR assessment.
  • ORR Annual Assessment: The Office of Rail and Road's verdict on NH performance. The Board fears this document. It measures compliance against the Licence, focusing on KPIs like 'Pavement Condition' (LARS data) and 'Structure Condition' (BCI). A poor assessment triggers DfT intervention.
Formal regulatory evaluation.

  • Road Investment Strategy (RIS) Efficiency KPI: The Treasury-mandated target to cut costs. Creates a perverse incentive to defer maintenance (lowering OPEX) and choose cheaper capital solutions that have higher whole-life costs, effectively mortgaging the future asset condition.
The formal contract with DfT.
Includes KPIs like 'P50 Network Availability' and 'Killed or Seriously Injured (KSI)' reduction.
Failure to meet these results in ORR enforcement action.
This drives the perverse incentive to prioritize interventions that boost the score over long-term asset health.

The data reveals a backlog of renewal needs that exceeds the allocated RIS3 operations budget, forcing a 'patch and mend' strategy.
The primary metric for road surface health; dictates renewals funding allocation; heavily criticized by regions for not reflecting the 'driver feel' of potholes, leading to a disconnect between central investment modelling and local repair needs.

  • KIM (Key Incident Management) Performance Metric: The internal metric tracking the timeline of major incidents. It specifically penalizes the 'slide' between estimated reopening times given to the media (via NTOC) and the actual handover time, highlighting the disconnect between on-road reality and control room estimation.
  • KPI: P50 Network Availability (97.5% Target): The primary operational metric for RIS2/RIS3 performance. It measures the percentage of the network available to traffic. Debriefs often devolve into arguments about 'start time' vs 'end time' codes in C&C logs, as a shift of 5 minutes in a major closure affects the regional P50 score. INCENTIVE RISK: Managers are incentivized to code incidents as 'Debris' rather than 'Infrastructure Failure' to protect availability stats.
  • 10-Minute Response Metric (ALR): The critical post-Stocktake performance metric: TOs must reach a stopped vehicle in a live lane on Smart Motorways within 10 minutes. This metric drives the positioning of 'Strategic Standby Points'. It creates a perverse incentive to cluster patrols on ALR sections (M1, M6, M25) at the expense of conventional motorways, leaving A-roads (A14, A303) with slower response times.
  • KPI: Clearance of Incidents < 1 Hour: The primary efficiency metric from the ORR delivery plan. Failure here results in 'Lost Customer Hours' penalties. This drives the 'drag and drop' culture—moving damaged vehicles to the hard shoulder or ERA rather than full recovery on scene—which sometimes conflicts with police forensic requirements at serious collisions.
  • P50 Planning Time Index Metric: Key operational performance metric measuring journey time reliability. Operations directorates are incentivized to hit this, which creates tension when Major Projects require lane closures that degrade this score.
  • KSI (Killed or Seriously Injured) Statistics: The ultimate safety metric reported to the ORR (Office of Rail and Road). The stagnation of KSI reduction on A-roads is driving a shift in focus from motorways to single-carriageway safety interventions in RIS3.
The ultimate safety metric.
The tension exists here: The statistic is lagging (takes months to validate via CRASH/STATS19), making it difficult to use for real-time operational decision-making or immediate intervention on accident blackspots.
  • Network Availability KPI (RIS3): The primary performance metric (target >97% lane availability). Severe weather closures directly penalize this metric unless classified as 'Force Majeure', leading to administrative friction between Delivery Directorates and ORR regarding event classification.
A critical RIS2/RIS3 performance metric derived directly from NTIS calculations of lane availability vs.
closure.
This metric drives funding and penalties.
There is a perverse incentive here: NTIS logic defines how 'available' the road is, meaning architectural defects in NTIS (e.g., failing to register a closure correctly due to sensor drop-out) can artificially inflate operational performance scores reported to the ORR (Office of Rail and Road).
  • ORR Safety Compliance Report: Annual regulatory stick used by the Office of Rail and Road. Specifically targets the '10-minute response time' KPI for stranded vehicles in live lanes. This metric drives the aggressive dispatch of Traffic Officers, sometimes at the expense of their own safety protocols during high-speed rolling road blocks.
  • Pavement Residual Life Calculation: Algorithmic assessment determining the structural remaining life of the carriageway. Influences the 'Depreciation' financial metric reported to DfT. Tension exists here: finance wants stable depreciation, engineering wants honest deterioration modelling which often shows accelerated aging on concrete sections (e.g., A14/A12).
  • Asset Data Quality Index (ADQI): The metric exposing the truth. Measures completeness, accuracy, and timeliness of asset data. Many legacy RIS1 schemes hold an ADQI below 80%, meaning Operations is maintaining the network based on assumptions rather than fact. Directly impacts the accuracy of 30-year renewal planning.
  • ORR Safety & Performance Review: Office of Rail and Road regulatory oversight. Scrutinizes NH's ability to predict asset failure. Poor ADMM compliance is a key finding in recent annual assessments, noting that NH cannot prove 'efficient expenditure' if it doesn't know the exact inventory of its assets.
  • Bridge Condition Index (BCI): The weighted average score of structure health. While the 'Average' BCI looks stable (approx 85-88), this masks a 'long tail' of critical sub-structures (piers, bearings) that are rated 'Poor' or 'Very Poor', posing operational risks to heavy load routes.
The key KPI reported to the ORR for structural health.
Current average (critical) score targets are under pressure due to the aging concrete stock from the 1970s motorway boom.

  • Macpherson Review (NSIP Operational Reform): 2023 review assessing the failure/success of Project Speed. Concluded that while NH accelerated submission, the Planning Inspectorate (PINS) and Statutory Consultees (Natural England, Environment Agency) became the bottleneck. Shifted focus from 'squeezing the timeline' to 'paying for consultee resource'.
  • Whole Life Costing (WLC) Model: The theoretical financial model supposed to balance Capex and Opex. In reality, often manipulated using optimistic maintenance assumptions (e.g., underestimating traffic management costs for steel barrier tensioning) to justify Capex cuts.
  • WebTAG Appraisal (BCR Calculation): The Treasury Green Book aligned appraisal methodology. Calculates the Benefit-Cost Ratio. Tension point: WebTAG historically undervalues resilience and technology renewals compared to journey time savings, often skewing the Route Strategy pipeline towards capacity schemes rather than necessary operational technology upgrades.
  • Asset Condition (BCI & Skid Resistance): Critical inputs for RIS3. Bridge Condition Index (BCI) and SCRIM (skid resistance) data. We are seeing a 'red wall' of aging concrete assets from the 1970s. The architectural tension is funding this unsexy maintenance against political desires for ribbon-cutting new bypasses.
Critical safety metric derived from TRACS/SCANNER surveys.
If P50 drops below investigatory levels, speed restrictions (TS 10 temporary speeds) must be applied.
A lagging indicator that often forces unplanned reactive maintenance.
  • Scope 3 Supply Chain Carbon Baseline: The aggregate carbon footprint of the Extended Supply Chain. Data quality is low (confidence <0.6) because Tier 2/3 suppliers often estimate emissions using spend-based proxies rather than Environmental Product Declarations (EPDs). This creates a 'blind spot' in the architecture where we report compliance to DfT based on modeled rather than actual data.
  • GG 104 Safety Risk Assessment (Innovation): The critical pass/fail node. Any new technology affecting the SRN must prove safety equivalence under DMRB GG 104. This is the primary bottleneck for AI/Machine Learning adoption, as deterministic safety cases struggle to validate non-deterministic probabilistic AI outputs.
The critical safety assurance process mandated by DMRB GG 104.
This assessment is currently a bottleneck for the M6 J21a-26 Smart Motorway upgrade, where the deviation from standard regarding Emergency Refuge Area (ERA) spacing is under intense scrutiny following the Transport Select Committee recommendations.
  • Micromobility Safety Evidence Stocktake (STATS19 Data): The accumulation of accident data derived from CRASH and COPA systems during the trials. Critical findings revealed a disproportionate severity of injuries at higher speeds (>15.5mph) and significant conflict points at uncontrolled crossings. For NH, the key metric was the 'pavement clutter' risk from delivery bots and the instability of e-scooters on high-speed A-road verges, directly influencing the rejection of 'free-floating' models near the SRN.
  • KPI: P50 (Clearance of Incidents): Operational metric measuring the time to clear 50% of incidents. Heavily scrutinized by ORR. Direct tension with 'Forensic Collision Investigation' requirements which require road closures to be maintained for police evidence gathering.
The Holy Grail metric: % of incidents cleared within 1 hour.
This drives behavior.
Traffic Officers may prioritize quick clearance (towing to hard shoulder) over forensic data collection, impacting root cause analysis.
  • Legacy Data Fragmentation Gap: The critical architectural debt. Asset data lives in HASS/IAM IS (static), traffic data in NTIS (dynamic), and major project data (A428, LTC) in BIM silos. There is no common data environment that currently satisfies the 'Single Source of Truth' requirement for a functioning Digital Twin.
