  • Verify Highways Common Induction (HCI): The process of validating that all supply chain workforce personnel possess a valid HCI card/passport before accessing the strategic road network (SRN). This ensures competency and safety awareness in line with 'Home Safe and Well' principles.
  • Administer NEC4 Contract Compensation Events: The management of cost and time changes within the NEC4 Engineering and Construction Contract. Used on major projects like the A428 Black Cat to Caxton Gibbet to agree on the financial impact of scope changes or unforeseen risks.
  • Conduct Route Strategy Analysis: The cyclical process of analyzing the performance of the SRN across 18 defined routes to identify constraints, safety hotspots, and future capacity needs to inform RIS3 planning.
  • Define RIS Digital Requirements: The strategic process of determining digital infrastructure needs for upcoming Road Investment Strategy (RIS3) periods. Involves analyzing DfT mandates and gaps in the SRN connectivity, specifically for schemes like the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine and Lower Thames Crossing.
  • Design ITS in Compliance with DMRB: Developing technical designs for Intelligent Transport Systems adhering to the Design Manual for Roads and Bridges. Specifically applies GG 184 (Specification for ITS) and CD 109 (Highway link design) to ensure standardisation across Smart Motorways and Expressways.
  • Install Roadside Technology Assets: Physical installation of digital assets on the network. Includes cabling, gantry erection, and mounting of radar/cameras. Requires coordination with Traffic Management to minimize LARS (Lane Availability Reporting System) impact during works.
  • Integrate with National Traffic Information Service (NTIS): Configuring data flows from roadside sensors (loops/radar) to the NTIS cloud environment. Ensures real-time traffic data is available for the National Network Management Centre (NNMC) and third-party data consumers.
  • Commission Assets into HART/CHARM: The technical onboarding of devices into the Traffic Management System (currently transitioning from legacy systems to HART). Ensures Regional Control Centres (RCCs) have command and control over the new digital signals and signs.
  • Handover to Regional Operations: The formal transfer of digital assets from the Major Projects Delivery Team to Operations Directorate. Involves populating the IAM-IS (Integrated Asset Management Information System) and training Traffic Officers on new capabilities.
  • Perform GG 119 Road Safety Audit: Execution of formal safety audits at Design (Stage 1/2), Opening (Stage 3), and Monitoring (Stage 4) phases. Mandatory for all improvement schemes like A428 Black Cat.

  • Board Chair: Currently Dipesh Shah. The primary interface with the DfT Permanent Secretary and Ministers. His role is less about roads and more about ensuring the 'Framework Document' is adhered to. He arbitrates the tension between the CEO's operational reality and the DfT's political aspirations for the SRN.
  • Chief Executive Officer (CEO): Nick Harris. Acts as the Accounting Officer (AO) for National Highways. He has personal liability to Parliament for the proper stewardship of public funds. He sits on the Board but answers to it. His primary headache is balancing the ORR's efficiency KPIs (KP1) against the safety imperatives of GG 104.
  • National Vehicle Recovery Manager (NVRM) Contractor: Outsourced recovery service (e.g., FMG Support) activated when private recovery is failing or dangerous. Statutory removal powers. Trade-off: High cost to NH for activation vs. cost of congestion. Metric: 'Time to Hook' typically <30 mins required by contract.
  • Technical Response Group (TRG): Maintenance contractor teams (e.g., Kier, Amey) deployed for heavy asset interaction: cone laying, barrier repair, fluid spill remediation. Friction: TRG mobilization times (often 60+ mins) frequently blow incident resolution KPIs compared to rapid TO response.
  • National Incident Liaison Officer (NILO): Based at NTOC (Quinton), responsible for strategic oversight of major incidents. They bridge the gap between tactical RCC command and DfT/Ministerial reporting. During debriefs, NILOs enforce the 'National Operating Instructions' against local RCC operational shortcuts.
  • On-Road Traffic Officer (ORTO): Frontline operative role holding specific powers under the Traffic Management Act 2004. Unlike generic 'patrols', this role is strictly governed by 'Concept of Operations' (ConOps) for specific road types (Dynamic Hard Shoulder vs. ALR). Accountability gap: ORTOs are often first-on-scene at fatal incidents, creating high PTSD risk (Occupational Health dependency) and reliance on the 'Trauma Risk Management' (TRiM) process, which is currently under-resourced.
Frontline patrol units operating under the Traffic Management Act 2004.
Unlike police, they lack enforcement powers but are essential for reaching P50 incident clearance targets.
High turnover rates in regions like the South East impact operational capability.

  • Office of Rail and Road (ORR) Monitor: The independent regulator holding National Highways to account. They are increasingly scrutinizing the 'Efficiency' of renewals, challenging why unit costs for asphalt vary wildly between Area 7 (East Mids) and Area 10 (North West).

  • Principal Designer (PD): Statutory role coordinating health and safety in the pre-construction phase. On the Smart Motorway Alliance (SMA), this role struggles to reconcile legacy as-built data (often missing from GDMS) with new ALR design requirements.
  • Principal Contractor (PC): Statutory role planning, managing, and monitoring the construction phase. For the M6 J21a-26 upgrade, the PC is liable for site safety. They control the 'Construction Phase Plan' but often face pressure from NH Operations to minimize lane closures (Chapter 8 traffic management) to maintain network availability.
  • Regional Control Centre (RCC) Operator: Staff based in centres like Godstone or Quinton. High cognitive load monitoring HART and CCTV for incident detection. Sedentary role with significant psychological stress from managing life-or-death incidents remotely.
Frontline operational staff at locations like RCC Godstone and RCC Wakefield.

Lacks competency to interpret probabilistic CAV data feeds or manage 'cooperative' traffic management plans, creating a bottleneck for deploying Connected Corridor use cases.

  • Independent Tunnel Safety Officer (TSO): A statutory role that must be functionally independent from the Tunnel Manager (Operations). This creates deliberate organizational friction. The TSO for the A3 Hindhead has the authority to recommend suspension of operations if safety documentation (GG 104) isn't ALARP. In practice, this role often clashes with the 'Keep Traffic Moving' directive during complex maintenance windows.
  • On-Road Traffic Officer: The human reality check for digital failure. When SVD radar throws a false positive or a smart motorway signal sticks, these officers manage the live lane risk. There is significant cultural friction between their operational reality and the 'Digital Roads' utopian rhetoric coming from Bridge House.
Frontline operational role enforcing closure compliance and incident management.
Dependent on inaccurate HART/CHARM signaling data during 'limbo' periods of scheme handover.
The boots on the ground enforcing lane closures and managing incidents.

Patrol units responsible for clearing incidents, managing traffic, and supporting road users, requiring constant connectivity via TORS and mobile data terminals.
  • On-Road Traffic Officer Service (East Region): Frontline operational response units. Statutory powers under Traffic Management Act 2004. Currently facing resource constraints covering A14/A428 works while maintaining response times to P1 incidents.
On-road responders for A428 and M11.
Safety critical role acting under the Traffic Management Act 2004.

  • ITS Systems Assurance Engineer: Scarce role responsible for validating safety-critical software updates under DMRB GG 104 requirements. Current headcount is insufficient to handle the velocity of software changes required for V2X integration on the Lower Thames Crossing, leading to reliance on external consultants and loss of intelligent client capability.
  • National Traffic Operations Centre (NTOC) Operator: The frontline role managing real-time operational risk. They execute the 'Response' phase of the risk framework, setting signals on the NTIS system. Their workload is a risk factor itself; operator fatigue leads to delayed signal setting during incidents on the M1.
  • Compliance Officer (Oversight & Compliance): Functions like Safety, Engineering & Standards (SES) and Net Zero that set frameworks (DMRB, GG 104) and monitor compliance. A critical architectural tension exists here: the Second Line often lacks the capacity to physically inspect all First Line assets, relying heavily on self-certification by project teams.
  • Senior Responsible Owner (SRO): The single point of accountability for a major scheme (e.g., A428 Black Cat). In reality, this role faces a massive tension: they are accountable for delivery under the OSM (Operational Scheme Manual) but often lack direct line management control over the matrixed technical assurance teams (SES) required to sign off the design, creating a critical bottleneck in the governance flow.
  • Traffic Officer Service (TOS): On-road operational resource responding to incidents; their safety is the primary driver for 'Red X' compliance enforcement; currently facing morale issues due to the increased risk profile of ALR (Smart Motorways) without hard shoulders.
  • First Line of Defence (Operational Risk Ownership): Operational management within Operations and Major Projects directorates who own and manage risks day-to-day. They are responsible for implementing controls (e.g., traffic management via RCCs) and delivering schemes (e.g., A428, A66) in line with DMRB standards. In reality, delivery pressure often conflicts with assurance processes here.
  • RCC Traffic Assessment Officer (TAO): Operational staff within the Control Room (e.g., RCC West Midlands) responsible for monitoring MIDAS alerts and CCTV. They utilise HART's incident management interface to set 'Red X' closures for stopped vehicles in ALR (All Lane Running) sections. Their workflow is heavily scrutinised following the ORR 'Smart Motorways Evidence Stocktake', placing immense pressure on HART's UI responsiveness during high-stress incidents.
  • Delivery Integration Partner (DIP): Tier 1 contractors (e.g., Balfour Beatty, Galliford Try) appointed under RDP. They hold the risk for design and construction but rely heavily on a transient Tier 2/3 supply chain, often creating a visibility gap regarding quality assurance and modern slavery compliance.
  • On-Road Traffic Officer Service (TOS): Frontline operational response. Role has shifted significantly from 'traffic management' to 'incident safety' following the removal of hard shoulders on ALR (All Lane Running) schemes. Primary users of the Airwave radio network.
Uniformed officers with statutory powers under the Traffic Management Act 2004 to stop traffic, close lanes, and manage incidents on the SRN to protect the scene and restore capacity.
  • Maintenance and Response Contractor: Supply chain partners (Asset Delivery Community) contracted to execute physical works, including cyclic maintenance, winter service, and defect repair, operating under the Asset Delivery model.
  • Road Safety Audit Team: Independent team responsible for conducting Stage 1-4 Road Safety Audits (RSA) in accordance with GG 119, ensuring distinct separation from the design team.

ARCHIMATE:BUSINESSSERVICE (78 components):
----------------------------------------
  • National Traffic Data Publication Service: The external dissemination of SRN status via DATEX II v3 feeds. Critical for meeting the 'Open Data' requirements of the DfT Protocol. Consumers include Google Maps, Waze, and logistics firms. Operational issue: There is a latency gap between an incident being verified by a Traffic Officer (Airwave radio) and that status appearing in the DATEX feed, often leading to Waze showing a closure before the official NH feed does.
  • Project Rapid (EV Charging Infrastructure): The £950m Rapid Charging Fund initiative to upgrade Motorway Service Areas (MSAs). Architectural constraint: National Highways does not own the MSAs (Moto, Welcome Break, etc.) nor the DNO grid connections. We are effectively funding assets we don't control, creating a governance void where we cannot enforce uptime reliability (99% availability) on the chargers despite public perception that it's 'our' responsibility.
  • Statutory Incident Information Publication: The legal obligation under the Highways Act 1980 and license conditions to inform the public of network availability. This service distinguishes 'verified' NH data from 'crowdsourced' Waze data. Performance is measured against KPI: Time to Inform (TTI) via VMS and Digital Channels.
  • Tunnel Incident Response Service: Delivered by dedicated Traffic Officers and local tunnel safety teams. Success metric: 'Time to Clear'. heavily dependent on the reliability of the PA/VA (Public Address/Voice Alarm) systems to instruct drivers to evacuate. If the technology fails, this service collapses, leading to potential loss of life.
  • NSIP Development Consent Order (DCO) Management: The critical path service for securing planning approval for major schemes like the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine and Lower Thames Crossing. This involves navigating the Planning Inspectorate process, managing Section 42 consultations, and mitigating Judicial Review risks. This service frequently clashes with engineering delivery teams who push for design flexibility after the 'Red Line Boundary' has been legally fixed.
  • Red Claims Recovery (Crown Property Damage): The revenue-generating legal service that chases insurers of drivers who damage SRN assets (barriers, bridges, gantries). There is a persistent operational conflict here: Traffic Officers (TOS) prioritize 'Clearance in 15 mins' (opening the road) to support P50 availability metrics, often destroying the forensic evidence Legal needs to pursue the claim.
  • Total Facilities Management (TFM) Contract: Outsourced provision of Hard FM (M&E maintenance) and Soft FM (security, cleaning). The friction point: SLA-driven maintenance often lags behind the immediate 'fix-on-fail' requirements of a live 24/7 control room environment, requiring escalation to Gold Command during failures.
  • Trauma Risk Management (TRiM): Peer-delivered mental health support system activated after 'Business Critical' incidents (e.g., multi-fatality collisions, suicides). Essential for maintaining staff availability in RCCs and Outstations post-incident.
  • Strategic Roads User Survey (SRUS) Management: The service managing the interface with Transport Focus to track driver satisfaction. The metrics derived here (journey time, safety perception, information quality) directly influence the RIS3 performance specification. There is a disconnect here where poor asset condition (potholes/LARS data) drives down satisfaction despite successful major scheme delivery.
  • Safety Critical Medical Screening: Mandatory 'Fitness for Task' occupational health checks (eyesight, cardiovascular, diabetes) for Traffic Officers. Failure results in immediate removal from driving duties, impacting regional shift coverage and LARS (Lane Availability) response times.
  • Lone Worker Monitoring Service: Technology-enabled welfare check for Inspectors and TOs operating remotely (e.g., inspecting drainage assets off-network). Relies on GPS devices/apps; failure creates unmitigated safety risk in remote areas like A66 Northern Trans-Pennine.
  • Strategic Road Network (SRN) Capacity Provision: The core service mandated by the Licence. Delivery is tensioned against the 'Safety First' imperative. Measured by Lane Availability Reporting System (LARS) but constantly degraded by Major Project interventions (e.g., A428, A66 construction).
  • SRN Open Data Integration Service (MaaS Enabler): Provides real-time traffic flow, incident, and roadwork data to third-party Mobility as a Service (MaaS) aggregators (Citymapper, Google, Logistics UK). Relies heavily on the National Traffic Information Service (NTIS) cloud migration. Critical friction point: Data granularity losses at the interface between SRN (Highways) and Local Road Networks (Local Authorities), often causing 'blind spots' in end-to-end journey planning.
  • Connected & Autonomous Vehicle (CAV) Infrastructure Readiness: Service capability to support Autonomous Mobility on Demand (AMoD). Focuses on physical and digital infrastructure certification for Level 3/4 autonomy. Heavily constrained by the 'Smart Motorways Evidence Stocktake' safety criteria. Currently piloting on the A2/M2 Connected Corridor, but national rollout is stalled by funding tensions between RIS3 digital enhancements and basic asset renewal needs.
  • Autonomous Freight Corridor Optimization (Logistics): A specialized service prioritizing heavy freight platooning and autonomous logistics flow, specifically targeting the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine and A14 Cambridge to Huntingdon corridors. Aims to smooth flow to reduce braking/emissions. Trade-off: Requires reserving dynamic capacity (virtual lanes) which conflicts with general traffic capacity KPIs (P50 journey times) during peak hours.
  • SRN Dynamic Asset Monetisation (IaaS): Future capability to charge for specific infrastructure usage (e.g., dynamic tolling for premium express lanes or EV charging slot reservation). Currently technically feasible via free-flow charging (like Dart Charge), but politically toxic. Architecturally limited by the legacy interfaces in the payment processing systems and strict Treasury constraints on hypothecated funding.
  • Independent Assurance Service (TAS): Provided by Safety, Engineering and Standards (SES) directorate. They act as the internal regulator. There is a structural conflict here: The Major Projects directorate (Delivery) wants speed; SES (Assurance) wants absolute adherence to DMRB standards like CD 123 (Geometric design). Disputes here often escalate to the Chief Engineer.
  • Strategic Road Network Journey Service: The core product. Operational delivery is split between Regional Control Centres (RCCs) and on-road officers. The user experience is increasingly fragmented between 'Digital Roads' (Smart Motorways) and legacy A-roads (A47, A11).
  • Safety Improvement Programme Service: Identifies and delivers targeted engineering safety interventions
  • Safety Investigation Service: Provides incident analysis, reporting and recommendations
  • Worksite Safety Monitoring Service: Provides audits, inspections and compliance monitoring
  • Network Operations Control Service: Provides control-room monitoring and traffic interventions
  • Incident Response Service: Provides traffic management and incident clearance support
  • Live Journey Information Service: Provides updates via signs, apps, feeds and media channels
  • Network Inspection Service: Provides scheduled inspections and condition reporting
  • Asset Renewal Delivery Service: Provides resurfacing and infrastructure renewal works
  • Emergency Maintenance Service: Provides urgent repair and defect response
  • Infrastructure Planning Service: Provides feasibility, modelling and option appraisal
  • Capital Scheme Delivery Service: Provides construction and commissioning of improvements
  • Asset Commissioning Service: Provides acceptance, testing and operational readiness support
  • Customer Contact Service: Provides enquiries, complaints and engagement handling
  • Public Information Service: Provides alerts, campaigns and road-user communications
  • Journey Planning Data Service: Provides network data feeds and information services
  • Environmental Monitoring Service: Provides reporting on environmental performance
  • Environmental Mitigation Service: Provides environmental improvement programmes
  • Community Liaison Service: Provides consultations and local engagement activities
  • Procurement Service: Provides sourcing and tender management
  • Supplier Performance Service: Provides contract monitoring and performance reporting
  • Supply Chain Assurance Service: Provides compliance audits and governance reporting
  • Strategic Planning Service: Provides strategy development and scenario modelling
  • Regulatory Reporting Service: Provides reporting to government and regulators
  • Investment Portfolio Service: Provides prioritisation and investment oversight
  • National Highways Board: Governs organisation and reports to Secretary of State
  • Chief Executive Office: Leads organisational execution and delivery
  • Customer & Strategy Directorate: Defines customer strategy, planning and policy
  • Finance Directorate: Manages budgets, reporting, and value for money
  • Major Projects Directorate: Builds new road schemes and upgrades
  • Safety, Engineering & Standards Directorate: Maintains engineering policy and standards
  • Regional Operations Divisions: Run maintenance, asset management and repairs
  • National Traffic Operations Service: Monitors network and manages incidents
  • Traffic Officer Service: Patrols roads and manages disruptions
  • Digital & Information Directorate: Provides digital, cyber and data services
  • Data & Analytics Services: Supports decision-making with analytics
  • Commercial Directorate: Manages contracts and supplier relationships
  • HR Directorate: Provides people management and workforce planning
  • Communications & Corporate Affairs: Handles public messaging and stakeholder relations
  • Regional Director Offices: Provide regional governance and coordination
  • Regional Control Centre (RCC) Operations: 24/7 operational service provided by on-duty operators at ROCs (e.g., Godstone, South Mimms, Wakefield). Responsible for interpreting incoming alarms from MIDAS/SVD and visual verification via CCTV before dispatching Traffic Officers or setting VMS signals.
  • Traffic Monitoring Service: The operational service provided by Operations Directorate to ensure network availability and safety. governed by GG 104 (Safety Risk Assessment) standards to ensure risks are ALARP (As Low As Reasonably Practicable).
  • Abnormal Indivisible Load (AIL) Routing: A statutory service (Electronic Service Delivery for Abnormal Loads - ESDAL) allowing hauliers to plot routes for loads exceeding standard dimensions/weights. The service relies on accurate structural capacity data to prevent damage to bridges and flyovers.
  • Statutory Planning Consultation Service: The interface provided to the Planning Inspectorate, Local Authorities, and the public during the DCO application process. Facilitates the submission of Environmental Statements, consultation responses, and examination evidence.
  • Traffic Officer Response Service: The 24/7/365 rapid response service delivered by on-road Traffic Officers and Regional Control Centres (RCCs). Provides incident management, rolling road blocks, and clearance of carriageway obstructions to restore Network Availability and ensure safety under the Traffic Management Act 2004.
  • Traffic Information Provision Service: The dissemination of real-time traffic data to road users via Variable Message Signs (VMS), the Traffic England website, and third-party data feeds (Datex II). Relies on the National Traffic Information Service (NTIS) to provide journey planning and congestion alerts.
  • Strategic Road Network Enhancement Service: The delivery of major capital improvement schemes defined in the Road Investment Strategy (RIS2/RIS3), such as the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine and Lower Thames Crossing. Involves Development Consent Order (DCO) applications and Nationally Significant Infrastructure Project (NSIP) delivery.
  • SRN Asset Maintenance Service: Routine and cyclical maintenance of physical assets (pavement, structures, drainage, technology). Ensures assets meet DMRB standards (e.g., CS 450 for structures) and remain safe for use, addressing defects like potholes and barrier damage.
  • Incident Management Service: The coordination of Traffic Officer Service (TOS) and emergency response to unplanned events on the Strategic Road Network (SRN). This service ensures compliance with the 1-hour lane clearance KPI mandated in the DfT/NH Delivery Plan and supports the 'Safety' outcome of RIS2. It operates 24/7/365 from Regional Control Centres (RCCs) and the National Traffic Operations Centre (NTOC).
  • Strategic Traffic Information Service: Provision of real-time and predictive network status information to road users, logistics providers, and third-party aggregators (SatNav providers). This service fulfills statutory obligations to inform the public of network availability and supports the RIS2 'Customer' outcome by improving journey time reliability (measured by Delay metrics).
  • Abnormal Indivisible Load (AIL) Management Service: The processing, authorisation, and routing of vehicles exceeding standard dimensions/weights (STGO) across the SRN. This service ensures structural safety of bridges and gantries (DMRB assessment standards) and minimizes traffic disruption during heavy haulage movements.
  • Asset Condition Monitoring Service: Continuous surveillance and data analysis of pavement, structures, and roadside technology assets. Uses data from SCANNER surveys and TRACS to inform the Pavement Renewal Programme and ensure compliance with DMRB CS 228 (Skidding Resistance) and CS 450 (Inspection of Highway Structures).
The service utilizing SCANNER and TRACS surveys to measure ride quality, rutting, and cracking across the SRN pavement assets.
  • Road Space Booking Service: The coordination of network occupancy for maintenance, major projects (e.g., A66, Lower Thames Crossing), and statutory undertakers. This service minimizes conflict between simultaneous RIS schemes and maximizes P50 network availability.
  • Incident Response and Clearance Service: The end-to-end operational service provided by National Highways to detect, respond to, and clear incidents on the Strategic Road Network (SRN). This service targets the 'CLEAR' (Collision, Lead, Evaluate, Act, Re-open) initiative objectives to minimize lane unavailability and maximize journey time reliability as per RIS2/RIS3 performance specifications.
  • Incident Detection and Verification Service: The operational service of identifying unplanned events on the network using MIDAS, SVD, and CCTV, ensuring compliance with the 20-second detection targets for stopped vehicles on Smart Motorways.
  • Severe Weather Management Service: The activation of severe weather protocols (e.g., CRISP, salt spreading) based on Met Office data and road weather sensors to maintain skid resistance and network availability during snow, ice, or flooding.
  • Statutory Consultation Service: The provision of formal public consultation mechanisms required under the Planning Act 2008 for Nationally Significant Infrastructure Projects (NSIPs). Ensures local communities and statutory bodies (Natural England, Historic England) feed into scheme designs (e.g., A428 Black Cat to Caxton Gibbet). Failure in this service risks Judicial Review.
  • Noise Insulation Scheme Administration: The service managing eligibility and installation of noise insulation for properties affected by new schemes or excessive noise levels, pursuant to the Noise Insulation Regulations 1975. Directly addresses community impact for residents near major projected works like the A12 Chelmsford to A120 widening.
  • Structural Integrity Assessment Service: Provision of Principal Inspections (6-yearly) and General Inspections (2-yearly) for bridges and tunnels, ensuring compliance with DMRB CS 450.
  • Incident-Led Repair Service: Operational service to deploy maintenance crews to fix immediate hazards identified by Traffic Officers or public reports, adhering to GM 701 response times.
  • National Highways Customer Contact Centre Service: 24/7/365 contact service handling public inquiries, reporting of defects (potholes, debris), and complaints, serving as the primary interface for non-emergency customer interaction.

ARCHIMATE:CAPABILITY (87 components):
-----------------------------------
  • V2I Data Exchange Capability: The organizational ability to transmit safety-critical data (GLOSA, RWW - Road Works Warning) between National Highways infrastructure and vehicles. Currently constrained by legacy UTMC (Urban Traffic Management Control) latencies and the fragmentation between regional RCCs and the National Traffic Information Service (NTIS).
  • Predictive Network Operations Capability: The organizational ability to foresee network disruption before it occurs. Currently low maturity; we rely on reactive measures via NTOC. The target is to use AI to predict flow breakdown (Smart Motorways Evidence Stocktake requirement) rather than just detecting it via MIDAS loops.
  • SRN Level 4/5 Automation Readiness (CAV Enablement): The ability of the Strategic Road Network to support SAE Level 4/5 automated driving systems (ADS) without human fallback. This represents a fundamental shift from 'passive infrastructure' to 'digitally cooperative infrastructure'. Current tension: RIS3 funding prioritizes renewal of existing assets over digital upgrades, creating a gap between 'Digital Roads' vision and operational reality on corridors like the M1 and M6.
  • SRN Business Continuity & Resilience: The ability to maintain Strategic Road Network (SRN) operations during disruptive events (cyber-attack, severe weather, physical infrastructure failure). Encompasses compliance with Civil Contingencies Act 2004 and ISO 22301, but practically focuses on keeping the RCCs operational and Smart Motorways (ALR) safe when technology fails.
  • Digital Twin & Asset Analytics Capability: The organizational ability to leverage data from HART (Highway Architecture for Real-time Traffic) and asset condition surveys (TRACS/SCANNER) to predict failure (P50 pavement life) rather than reacting to potholes. Currently immature due to data silos.

ARCHIMATE:CONSTRAINT (63 components):
-----------------------------------
  • Smart Motorway Evidence Stocktake (2020) & Written Ministerial Statement: A hard political constraint that paused the rollout of All Lane Running (ALR) schemes. It overrides previous architectural roadmaps and forces a retrofit of Stopped Vehicle Detection (SVD) radar to existing schemes (M1, M6), diverting funds from planned RIS2 enhancements.
  • Highways Act 1980 Section 41 (Duty to Maintain): The absolute statutory floor. Section 41 imposes a duty to maintain the highway at public expense. This is not optional. Failure here leads to direct legal liability for National Highways. This forces Operations to prioritise reactive patching (potholes) over strategic asset management when OpEx is tight, creating a 'fix on fail' culture despite asset management rhetoric.
  • Infrastructure Act 2015 Part 4 (RIS Implementation): Establishes the Road Investment Strategy (RIS) legal framework. It separates NH (License Holder) from DfT (Shareholder). While intended to provide 5-year funding certainty, it creates a rigid capital cycle (RIS2/RIS3) that often conflicts with the fluid reality of asset degradation and inflationary pressures on schemes like the A66.
  • DfT Framework Document: The foundational governance contract that dictates what the Board can and cannot do. It specifically limits the Board's borrowing powers and mandates compliance with the Green Book for investment appraisals. It creates a rigid dependency loop where NH cannot deviate from agreed RIS outcomes without lengthy DfT Change Control.
  • DMRB GG 104 (Safety Risk Assessment): The overarching safety standard. Every change to TOS operations (e.g., single crewing trials) must demonstrate 'As Low As Reasonably Practicable' (ALARP) risk profiles under GG 104. This standard is currently the primary blocker to operational cost-saving initiatives, as proving safety neutrality on ALR sections is statistically difficult.
The 'Bible' for safety governance.
Any deviation from standard on A428 or A66 requires a GG 104 assessment.
Post-Smart Motorway stocktake, the bar for 'As Low As Reasonably Practicable' (ALARP) has effectively been raised to 'Eliminate Risk' by the ORR.
The 'Safety Bible'.
This is not a guideline; it is the statutory safety governance standard.
Every major project must produce a GG 104 compliant Safety Risk Assessment.
This defines the safety baseline.
Currently, there is significant friction applying GG 104 to 'Digital Roads' initiatives where software failure modes are not adequately covered by traditional civil engineering hazard logs.
The 'Safety Bible' for the Strategic Road Network (SRN).
Mandates the ALARP (As Low As Reasonably Practicable) approach.
Currently the primary friction point for Smart Motorway (ALR) retrofits, as proving safety equivalency against hard shoulder baselines requires complex data evidence from SVD (Stopped Vehicle Detection) systems.
The governing standard for safety risk on the SRN.
This is the 'governor' on the speed of HART deployment.
Every migration from NRTS to HART requires a GG 104 safety assessment to prove that the change in transmission technology does not increase the risk of a fatality (FSI) on smart motorways.
The governing standard for safety risk.
Any change to the SCADA code (even a patch) requires a full GG 104 assessment, slowing down the software update cycle from 'Agile' sprints to 6-month waterfall releases.
The absolute governing standard for safety risk on the SRN.
No scheme, digital or physical, goes live without a GG 104 safety case.
The tension: GG 104 is deterministic and struggles to quantify the stochastic behavior of AI/Machine Learning in CAVs.
We are effectively forcing probabilistic AI risk into a deterministic engineering box.
Requires ALARP (As Low As Reasonably Practicable) demonstration for any operational change or departure from standard.
Strict adherence to GG 104 is currently slowing down digital innovation pilots as safety cases for non-standard AI traffic detection take 12-18 months to approve.
The primary safety governance standard.
Any CAV trial (e.g., platooning) requires a rigorous GG 104 safety case.
This creates operational friction as 'agile' digital teams struggle with the deterministic safety evidence required by the Safety Engineering & Standards (SES) directorate.
  • RIS2/RIS3 Budget Envelope: The fixed 5-year funding settlement from DfT. Inflation (construction materials index) has eroded real purchasing power, forcing a trade-off: cancelling 'desirable' preventative works to fund 'essential' safety-critical renewals, contradicting the whole-life cost efficiency mandate.
  • Performance Specification (P50): The metric requiring 98% of lanes to be available. This creates a perverse incentive to patch-repair (potholes) rather than perform deep structural renewals, as full renewals require longer possession times that hurt the P50 score.
  • DMRB CS 450 Inspection of Highway Structures: Mandates the cycle of General and Principal Inspections (6-yearly). Compliance here is non-negotiable for safety, but the output (General Inspection Reports) often sits in a backlog because there isn't enough Opex budget to fix the 'Category 2' defects identified, creating a liability paper trail.
DMRB standard mandating the frequency and method of structural inspections to ensure the safety of bridges, gantries, and retaining walls.
  • DMRB CS 228 Skidding Resistance: Standard defining the Investigatory Levels (IL) for skid resistance. This standard forces immediate intervention if SCRIM coefficients drop below threshold, overriding planned capital works and disrupting the 5-year forward programme. A primary driver for emergency resurfacing.
The standard mandating friction levels.
Failure to meet this triggers immediate SCRIM/SCANNER alerts.
Often forces emergency resurfacing that Operations hates because it disrupts flow on strategic corridors.
Mandatory Design Manual for Roads and Bridges (DMRB) standard governing the management of skidding resistance on the SRN.
It dictates investigatory levels for friction based on site categories (e.g., approaches to junctions, free-flow motorways).
  • Asset Data Management Manual (ADMM) v2.2: The mandatory standard defining data requirements for SRN assets. Specifies attributes for Pavement (HAPMS), Structures (SMIS), and Geotech (GDMS). Often treated as a 'tick-box' exercise by Major Projects supply chains, leading to data gaps at PCF Stage 6 (Construction end). Governance sits with SES (Safety, Engineering & Standards).
The rigid data dictionary that defines how National Highways classifies assets (from gantry foundations to drainage nodes).
This creates a massive architectural tension: modern BIM models use IFC (Industry Foundation Classes) or Uniclass 2015, but ADMM requires specific internal codes for ingestion into IAM IS.
This translation layer is where 30-40% of data fidelity is lost during handover.
The data standard governing asset attributes.
Frequently bypassed by supply chain contractors in the rush to meet 'Open for Traffic' deadlines, resulting in 'digital debt' for Asset Management.
  • Road Investment Strategy 2 (RIS2) Capital Envelope: The £27.4bn funding constraint (2020-2025) which is currently over-subscribed due to construction inflation. This creates a hard tension: funds must be diverted from 'Renewal of Roads' (Opex/Capex mix) to plug gaps in flagship Enhancement schemes like the A66 Northern Trans-Pennine, starving the asset base of necessary maintenance.
  • Constraint: Implied element created to satisfy AI-discovered relationship
  • DMRB CS 551 (Testing and inspection of drainage systems): Specifies the inspection frequency and testing standards. Creates a heavy resource burden on Operations Directorate to validate asset condition, often leading to a backlog of required CCTV surveys which constrains accurate investment modelling.
  • Smart Motorway Stocktake (2020) & Pause (2022): DfT mandated pause on new ALR schemes until 5 years of safety data is available. Forces MPD to pivot resources from new builds (M3 J9) to maintenance and safety retrofits.
Government mandate halting new ALR schemes.
This has stranded capital assets (gantries, barriers) on paused schemes like the M3 J9-14, forcing a complex architectural pivot to retrofit existing ALR capacity with additional emergency areas (ERAs) rather than delivering new capacity.
Government instruction halting new ALR schemes.
This stranded millions in sunk costs for architecture designed for Smart Motorways (e.g., specific cabling infrastructure on the M3) that now must support a 'Dynamic Hard Shoulder' or traditional layout, leaving architectural 'orphans' in the roadside cabinet network.
  • ORR Safety Reporting Requirements: Office of Road and Rail mandate to report on SVD performance (detection rates/time). If targets aren't met, ALR sections face potential closure or speed reduction.
  • Fixed Capex Funding Envelope: Hard budgetary ceiling for schemes like A66 Northern Trans-Pennine. Breaching this requires extensive internal governance (Investment Committee) and DfT approval, creating immense pressure to cut costs via material changes.
  • Government Pause on New Smart Motorways: DfT directive halting the rollout of new ALR schemes (removed from RIS2/3) until 5 years of safety data is available. This has orphaned several sunk costs in design and requires architectural rework of schemes like the M6 J21a-26 to revert to Dynamic Hard Shoulder or traditional widening.
DfT directive halting the roll-out of new All Lane Running schemes (e.g., M3 J9-14) until 5 years of safety data is gathered.
This has stranded capital investment and forced a shift to 'Retrofit ERA' programmes on existing RIS2 operational routes.
  • Smart Motorway Stocktake (2020/2022): The government response to Transport Committee recommendations effectively pausing All Lane Running (ALR) rollouts. This architectural constraint invalidates many historical Route Strategy options that relied on 'Cheap Capacity' via ALR, forcing a return to expensive widening or demand management.
  • PAS 2080:2023 Carbon Management in Infrastructure: The governing standard for managing whole-life carbon. While formally adopted, operational adherence varies. Major Projects (MP) apply it rigorously for DCO consent (e.g., Lower Thames Crossing), but smaller Operations (Ops) renewal schemes often bypass deep carbon analysis due to the 'constraints of existing alignment' loophole and the urgency of P1/P2 defect repairs.
The mandatory standard for carbon management capability.
We are certified, but the reality is a constant battle to force Tier 1 contractors on schemes like A66 Northern Trans-Pennine to move beyond 'tick-box' compliance to actual carbon engineering.
Requires explicit carbon baselining before Preliminary Design.
The global standard for managing carbon, adopted by NH.
It forces a 'whole life carbon' assessment.
The tension lies in the fact that while we certify against this, the actual supply chain (Tier 1 contractors on RIS schemes) struggles to provide granular data, making our carbon reporting largely estimated rather than measured.
  • DMRB Standards Rigidity (CD 123 / GG 101): Geometric Design (CD 123) and General Principles (GG 101) standards. These codify physical infrastructure requirements that often conflict with digital-first solutions (e.g., reducing physical gantries in favor of in-vehicle signaling), forcing hybrid costs without full benefits.
  • Planning Act 2008: Primary legislation. Imposes rigid 6-month examination limit which pressures NH teams to respond to 'Written Questions' within extremely tight deadlines (Deadlines 1-8).
The primary legislation governing NSIPs.
Sets the rigid statutory timelines that constrain National Highways' ability to iterate design once submitted.
Forces 'front-loading' of design work.
Legislation that mandates the use of Development Consent Orders (DCO) for Nationally Significant Infrastructure Projects (NSIPs) on the Strategic Road Network.
  • RIS2 Efficiency KPI (KPI4): Regulatory requirement to deliver £2.23bn efficiency savings. This creates a perverse incentive to defer Opex maintenance (Renewal of Roads) in favour of Capex capitalisation, leading to a degradation in long-term asset condition (skid resistance and pavement serviceability).
  • Carbon Budget & Net Zero 2050: Limits road capacity expansion in the RIS3 portfolio.
Legal constraint stopping road capacity expansion.
